<text>VODKA + SODA

F* white claw, YOU is the truth. Facts: real vodka in their soda (7.5%) compared to white claw no no real vodka only alcohol is the fermentation of the sugar.

The bar is cute and quaint. Came here for the Topo Chico and Tamales event, free Topo Chico but not free Tamales. That night they featured a small variety of Tamales to purchase, I had the strawberry tamale and it was good. Never had a pink tamale drizzled with condense milk until that night. I didn't order any of the special Topo Chico cocktails (ex: og, vodka, Topo Chico) because someone next to me referenced that cocktail took away the fizz of the Topo Chico.

In addition, my friends and I attended the Meat Ball and You & Yours was a vendor there. I had an unlimited amount of generous free pours of all their canned cocktail flavors (vodka mule, gin & tonic, vodka cranberry soda, key lime vodka soda). All were good but my favs were key lime vodka soda.

And You & Yours sells in some local grocery store. I was bummed to know that on weekdays they don't open until 4pm. I happen to stumble upon a case at Lazy Acres grocery store of my favorite Key Lime vodka soda. It's my go to drink when I go sailing!

Overall, good stuff. Kind of pricy but worth the buzz.<//text><Pics>None</Pics><resp>None< /resp><Gmap_id>0x80d9535e04a4ebaf:0xaba68288ea6eee92</Gmap_id></record></dataset><record>

< review>
Delicious craft cocktails on happy hour, but subpar service,  In addition to the seasonal summer cocktail menu, there's also a happy hour menu featuring a few of the cocktails. I'm glad my husband and I went with the happy hour menu - the drinks are essentially 50% off from $12 to $8.

The "Prized Pony" is a refreshing summer cocktail. It reminds of the Moscow Mule with vodka, ginger, lime, mint, and peach bitters.

"Do You Want That Spicy" cocktail has a spicy kick from the Serraro bitters. A strong Citrus flavor from the grapefruit, lime, and cucumber.

My husband and I enjoyed both drinks and going to get a 2nd round, but stopped short due to the lack of service. There was a big bachelor party that sat down before us and my husband and I patiently waited for 40 minutes to get our drinks. Once everyone in the party got their drinks and others were served at the bar, we walked up to the bar and were ignored by the bartenders. While I understand they are busy making drinks, they didn't acknowledge my husband and I until we requested to close out. They seemed apathetic and not welcoming.

Great distillery and cocktails, but be prepared to wait for them! The distillery allows dogs, so feel free to bring your furry friend.</review>

<Review>Regret working with this company: (Texcote Coolwall and stucco/wood repair) My experience: A sales representative was coming through the neighborhood offering services from the company and conveniently enough I was looking to have the exterior of my home redone so I set up an in person appointment with the company and they came out and gave an excellent and friendly overview of their painting and exterior repair services via another sales representative. They "offer" a 15% discount if you decide to go with them that day, otherwise you have to pay what they consider to be full price. I don't have much any complaints with the sales representatives as they were very friendly, although very pushy as well. The project manager introduced himself the following day and we discussed the timeline for when they would start. On the first day the crew came out and pressure washed the house without warning with my windows still open in some rooms so naturally dirty water got everywhere in those spaces while my wife frantically ran around stuffing towels underneath the doors as if a flood was happening because they were pressure washing under the front door as well. The next day they came out the immediately started applying the primer BEFORE they had done any repairs to the exterior stucco so I attempted to call the project manager and office multiple times to address this (The crew didn't speak English). Turns out my project manager had quit, and the company hadn't informed me of this so now I'm left to try to figure this out on my own. I finally got a call back 3 days later after the crew had already finished priming the home and my concern of why the priming occurred before the repairs was dismissed by the project manager, but somehow the crew managed to start repairing the exterior after this conversation. I want to note that the first few days of this project, nothing had been cleaned up from the yard, even though we were told (and reconfirmed with the project manager) that the crew would be cleaning up each day. Instead, at the end of each day, we had to clean up stucco and debris ourselves. We also had to pick up left over food that had been left by the crew a few times as well. At this point, ripped up stucco, massive amounts of peeling paint, and rotted wood has been primed over and I just know that it won't end up being the "new" looking house which the company advertised at this rate. The stucco repair was subpar (It just looks smeared like peanut butter rather than texture matched to the home and is very apparent), but at least the paint and trim itself doesn't look too bad. They didn't prime the repaired stucco and wood, rather just immediately started painting over it with the final paint. Massive amounts of over-spray all around the ground, on the patio, and on areas of concrete, but I all but had given up on trying to work with them at this point I just wanted all of this over with. The sales pitch team is great, the work is poor, and the communication was lousy. I felt like I was being scammed from start to finish. Additionally they claimed the paint would aid in reducing in home temperatures, but I set up temperature gauges inside and outside to see before and after, and the home is consistently hotter after the paint. For the price tag, we expected stellar work all around and that is just the opposite of what we got. The also emailed me loan docs at the end to sign, and then sent me the same loan docs already signed with my name on them with their IP address on it. (I didn't sign them myself)
